# Research Log

_One dated entry per day. Appended by /pre-market at 07:00 WIB. Optional midday addendum._
_Read by /market-open to determine execution plan. Never delete entries._

---

## 2026-04-19 (Sunday — simulation run)

### Macro Snapshot

| Indicator | Value | Change | Note |
|-----------|-------|--------|------|
| IHSG | 7,621 | +2.07% WoW | Up from 7,307 on Apr 9; +7.24% over past month; +18.38% YoY |
| IDR/USD | 17,115 | -0.97% MoM | Rupiah weakening; Apr range 16,870–17,194 |
| Newcastle coal (USD/ton) | 133.55 | -0.15% DoD | Retreating from Mar surge above $140; still +20% MoM |
| Palm oil (CPO, MYR/ton) | 4,450–4,580 | Sideways | Export volume down 30–39% in first 10 days Apr; oil rally partial offset |
| Nickel (USD/ton) | 17,635 | +2.7% vs Apr 1 | New HPM formula effective Apr 15 boosted sentiment; range $17,000–17,635 |
| Asia overnight (Apr 18) | Nikkei -1.75% (58,476); HSI -1.01%; CSI300 -0.17% | Profit-taking Fri after Thu surge | US-Iran deal optimism faded; Brent near $98 |
| Foreign flow (IDX) | Net SELL ~IDR 2–2.1T | Persistent outflow | Exception: BlackRock/JPMorgan added BBRI shares in Apr |

### Sector Momentum

| Sector | Trend | Notes |
|--------|-------|-------|
| Banking | BULLISH | BI rate held 4.75%; BBRI ex-div Apr 21 (IDR 209/share, 10.1% yield); BlackRock + JPMorgan accumulating; BBCA at 34% discount to 10-yr avg P/E |
| Coal / Energy | CAUTIOUSLY BULLISH | Newcastle up ~20% in Mar, now consolidating at $133; ITMG P/E 9.4x, yield 11%; DMO policy and output pressure cap upside |
| CPO / Agri | NEUTRAL-NEGATIVE | Exports weak (-30–39% early Apr); prices sideways at MYR 4,450–4,580; ringgit strength headwind |
| Property | NEUTRAL | BI holding rates limits immediate rate-cut catalyst; IDR weakness dents sentiment |
| Consumer | NEUTRAL | No immediate catalyst visible; IDR weakness pressures imported input costs |
| Telco | NEUTRAL | No data catalyst this week |

### Top 3 Candidates

#### 1. BBRI — Institutional accumulation + dividend yield play ahead of Apr 21 ex-date

- Thesis: BBRI is Indonesia's largest micro/SME lender trading at IDR 3,430 with a 10.1% dividend yield and a cash dividend of IDR 209/share going ex on April 21 — one of the most attractive income plays on the IDX right now.
- Thesis: BlackRock (19M shares) and JPMorgan (680K shares) both added in April, signaling that smart foreign money is accumulating despite the broader foreign outflow trend — a divergence that historically precedes a re-rating.
- Catalyst: Ex-dividend date April 21, 2026 (IDR 209/share); Q1 2026 earnings release April 29, 2026.
- Proposed entry: IDR 3,430 | Stop: IDR 3,190 (-7% cut-loss rule) | Target: IDR 3,900 (+13.7% upside)
- Conviction: HIGH

#### 2. ANTM — Policy-driven nickel ore price reset creates earnings upgrade cycle

- Thesis: Aneka Tambang is a state-owned miner with 18.1M wmt of nickel ore quota in 2026 (+12.7% YoY); the new ESDM HPM formula effective April 15 raised benchmark ore prices from ~$17/wmt to ~$40/wmt for 1.2% grade ore — a structural margin expansion that the market has not yet fully priced.
- Thesis: ANTM also has a gold production target of 935 kg (+25.8%) acting as a second revenue driver, and the stock is up 15.6% YTD with analyst targets at IDR 3,950, suggesting limited downside from current levels.
- Catalyst: New HPM Ministerial Decree No. 144 took effect April 15 — first full-quarter impact visible in Q2 results; nickel LME at $17,635 (multi-week high) adding to realization price tailwind.
- Proposed entry: IDR 3,940 | Stop: IDR 3,664 (-7%) | Target: IDR 4,600 (+16.8% upside, toward analyst TP of IDR 3,950–4,600)
- Conviction: MEDIUM-HIGH

#### 3. ITMG — Deep-value coal with 11% dividend yield; Newcastle rebound puts a floor under earnings

- Thesis: Indo Tambangraya Megah trades at only 9.4x trailing P/E with an 11.05% dividend yield — statistically cheap for a profitable exporter with no debt, at a time when Newcastle coal is holding above $130 after a 20%+ surge in March.
- Thesis: ITMG's next earnings (May 7) should reflect elevated Q1 coal prices, and with DMO-capped domestic sales, its export realizations in the $130+ range should translate to stronger-than-consensus margins.
- Catalyst: Q1 2026 earnings release May 7, 2026; continued coal price strength driven by supply tightness post-March surge.
- Proposed entry: IDR 27,050 | Stop: IDR 25,157 (-7%) | Target: IDR 31,500 (+16.4% upside)
- Conviction: MEDIUM

### Flagged Risks

- IDR/USD weakness (17,115 and trending toward 17,200) could prompt BI to intervene or signal hawkishness, weighing on rate-sensitive plays and equity multiples broadly.
- Foreign fund outflows remain persistent at ~IDR 2T net sell per week — a continuing headwind for index-level and large-cap liquidity; any escalation in outflows could trigger stop-outs.
- Asian markets showed sharp Friday profit-taking (Nikkei -1.75%, HSI -1%): if this carries into Monday open, IDX may gap down, creating adverse entry conditions for all three candidates.
- BBRI ex-dividend April 21 — stock will trade ex-div (adjusted down ~IDR 209) on that date; entry before ex-date carries dividend capture risk if price falls more than the dividend amount post ex-date.
- Newcastle coal has already surged 20%+ in March and is now consolidating; any downside surprise from China demand or Indian import data could cap ITMG upside quickly.
- Indonesia's CPO export volumes falling 30–39% early April — do not add AALI, LSIP, or agri exposure until exports recover.

### Plan for /market-open (Monday 2026-04-21)

- [ ] Monitor IHSG open direction: if gap-up or flat open, proceed with limit orders; if gap-down >0.5%, hold fire and reassess at 09:30 WIB
- [ ] BBRI: Place limit BUY at IDR 3,430 (or best offer within IDR 3,400–3,460 range). Position size: IDR 60,000,000 (20% of account). Note this is the ex-dividend date — confirm open price adjustment and adjust limit accordingly. Stop at IDR 3,190.
- [ ] ANTM: Place limit BUY at IDR 3,940 if stock holds above IDR 3,900 support at open. Position size: IDR 60,000,000 (20%). Stop at IDR 3,664. Do not chase above IDR 4,050.
- [ ] ITMG: Watch first 30 minutes of trading. If price holds IDR 27,000–27,200 range, place limit BUY at IDR 27,050. Position size: IDR 60,000,000 (20%). Stop at IDR 25,157.
- [ ] Do NOT open all 3 on the same day if market is weak at open — prioritize BBRI (highest conviction) first, ANTM second, ITMG third.
- [ ] Set 10% trailing stops on all filled positions immediately after execution.
- [ ] Cap total deployed capital at IDR 180,000,000 (3 positions × 20%) — leave IDR 120,000,000 in reserve.

### Top 3 Candidates

#### 1. ITMG — 114%-beat earnings + coal above $130 = deep-value re-rating

- Thesis: ITMG printed Q1 2026 EPS IDR 890 vs consensus IDR 416 — a 114% earnings beat — while still trading at ~9.4x P/E with 11% dividend yield. The market has not re-rated to reflect this earnings power, and the coal price floor ($130+) is intact.
- Thesis: Newcastle coal at $131–134 is holding above the $130 support level with a Middle East risk premium embedded; any analyst upgrade ahead of the May 7 official print could trigger rapid multiple expansion.
- Catalyst: Q1 EPS beat already public; May 7 official Q1 results filing; potential analyst upgrades in coming days.
- Proposed entry: IDR 27,000–27,200 | Stop: IDR 25,110 (10% trailing GTC) | Target: IDR 31,500 (+16.4%)
- Conviction: **HIGH** (upgraded — beat now confirmed via search)

#### 2. BBRI — Ex-dividend April 21 + institutional accumulation + Q1 earnings April 29

- Thesis: BBRI goes ex-dividend Monday April 21 (IDR 209/share cash, 10.1% annual yield); BlackRock added +19M shares and JPMorgan +680K shares in April — institutional accumulation against the foreign outflow trend.
- Thesis: Q1 2026 earnings release April 29 is the re-rating event; strong micro/SME loan growth and BI stability expected to support beat; US-Iran ceasefire reduces EM risk premium and benefits foreign flows back into Indonesia.
- Catalyst: Ex-dividend April 21 (stock adjusts down ~IDR 209 at open); Q1 earnings April 29.
- Proposed entry: IDR 3,200–3,250 (ex-div adjusted open) | Stop: IDR 2,990 (10% trailing GTC) | Target: IDR 3,700 (+14–16%)
- Conviction: **HIGH**

#### 3. ANTM — HPM nickel reform at $17,985/ton = structural margin upgrade not yet in price

- Thesis: ESDM Decree 144 (effective April 15) raised the nickel ore correction factor from 17% to ~30% for ANTM's 18.1M wmt of production — a structural margin expansion worth hundreds of billions in incremental EBITDA per quarter, not yet reflected in consensus estimates.
- Thesis: LME nickel now at $17,985 (+4.81% MoM, upgraded from prior $17,635 estimate) means both the HPM formula change AND the underlying nickel price are working in ANTM's favour simultaneously.
- Catalyst: First full-quarter impact of Decree 144 in Q2 2026 results (reported ~August); stock rose +1.03% to IDR 3,940 on Apr 15 announcement but has not fully discounted Q2 earnings impact.
- Proposed entry: IDR 3,900–3,960 | Stop: IDR 3,628–3,683 (10% trailing GTC) | Target: IDR 4,600 (+16.5%)
- Conviction: **MEDIUM-HIGH**

### Flagged Risks

- **BI rate cut scope shrinking**: Governor explicitly said cuts are "increasingly limited" due to IDR weakness and Middle East capital outflows. Removes near-term re-rating tailwind for BBRI and property; do not add property exposure.
- **Monday risk-ON vs Friday risk-OFF**: Asian markets sold off Friday (Nikkei -1.75%, HSI -1%); BUT US-Iran 2-week ceasefire announced with Strait of Hormuz reopening → Monday may gap UP on risk-on. Watch IHSG open vs 7,600 level.
- **BBRI ex-div gap**: Stock will open ex-div Monday (-IDR 209 adjustment). Entry price target shifts from IDR 3,430 to IDR 3,200–3,250. Stop set from actual fill, not pre-div price.
- **Foreign outflow weight**: Net foreign sell IDR 3.31T week of Apr 6–10; IDR 37.14T YTD. Persistent headwind on large-caps; any EM risk-off event could amplify selling.
- **CPO sector**: Exports -34–39% with no recovery signal — zero exposure to AALI, LSIP, or agri plays.
- **3-trade weekly limit**: All 3 trades planned for Monday April 21 would hit the weekly cap immediately. Priority: ITMG (highest conviction) → BBRI → ANTM.

### Top Candidates (score ≥ 6, deep-dive required)

#### 1. BBRI — Post-ex-div recovery with Q1 earnings catalyst Apr 29

**Fundamental case:**
- Thesis: BBRI is Indonesia's largest retail/micro lender with post-ex-dividend absorption complete. The recent dividend drop created a mechanical entry window at 3,220, and the stock has recovered to 3,480. Institutional accumulation (BlackRock, JPMorgan) provides support.
- Thesis: Q1 2026 earnings Apr 29 is the next re-rating event — 2026 guidance is NIM 7.4-7.8%, loan growth 7-9%, CIR 41-43%. A beat extends the bounce.
- Valuation: Q4 2025 EPS 105.13 (beat 98.34); trading ~2.1x P/B vs sector 2.3x.
- Catalyst: BI rate decision TODAY (Apr 22) — dovish surprise would push BBRI higher; hold at 4.75% already priced in.
- Analyst view: Consensus buy; TP range IDR 4,400-5,000.
- Insider activity: No material director transactions noted recently.

**Technical context:**
- Price: IDR 3,480 | 50-day MA est: ~3,300 | 200-day MA est: ~3,450
- Volume: broadly normal on ex-div recovery
- Support: IDR 3,270 (ex-div low) | Resistance: IDR 3,640 (pre-ex high)
- Trend: recovering from pullback; reclaimed 50-day MA

**Trade plan:**
- Entry: IDR 3,400-3,480 (current range) — do NOT chase above 3,510
- Hard cut: IDR 3,236 (-7%) | Target: IDR 3,780 (+8.6%)
- R:R: 1.23:1 — TIGHT. Marginal pass under 2:1 standard; prefer tighter entry
- Position size candidate: ~450,000 shares ≈ IDR 1.566B (15.7% equity) — flag: above regime 15% cap
- Adjust: cap at 425,000 shares ≈ IDR 1.479B (14.8%)
- Conviction: MEDIUM (catalyst near but R:R tight at current price)

#### 2. ANTM — HPM decree sustain; pullback provides better entry

**Fundamental case:**
- Thesis: ANTM is Indonesia's integrated nickel+gold miner. The HPM Decree 144 effective Apr 15 raises ore correction factor from 17% to 30% and adds Co/Fe/Cr to the HPM formula, lifting limonite ore HPM from ~$18/wmt to $35-40/wmt. ANTM 2026 production quota raised to 18.1M wmt (from 16.4M).
- Thesis: Dual tailwind — nickel ASP lift via HPM + gold price record highs support hedge.
- Valuation: Mid-cycle; integrated model supports premium to pure miners.
- Catalyst: HPM implementation updates; Q1 earnings date TBD.
- Analyst view: Upgrades from multiple houses post-HPM.

**Technical context:**
- Price: IDR 3,960 (pulled back from 4,070 high)
- Volume: elevated on HPM news
- Support: IDR 3,800 | Resistance: IDR 4,100
- Trend: uptrend; pullback to 38% retrace provides re-entry window

**Trade plan:**

- Conviction: MEDIUM-HIGH (HPM tailwind durable; entry acceptable)

### Macro Regime Assessment

**Regime: EM-OUTFLOW / RISK-CAUTIOUS (unchanged).**

- Reasoning: Foreign net sell continued IDR 791B even on a green IHSG day (+1.22%) — outflow regime intact. IDR sticky at 17,400 zone; 10Y SUN 6.81%. Q1 GDP 5.61% beat + April CPI 2.42% are cyclically positive but still net dovish for risk assets via BI-cut runway. Brent reversal -5.55% removes Mon's geopolitical premium and re-grounds the energy/coal complex on fundamentals, not war-headlines.
- Position sizing adjustment: max 15% per RISK-STATE.json (no relaxation). Defensive Quality track suspended (no qualifying valuation × σ data accessible — repeat constraint).
- What would shift to CONSTRUCTIVE: foreign-flow inflection (one week of net buy ≥ IDR 1T), IDR break below 17,000, IHSG reclaim 7,200, BI dovish pivot.

### Flagged Risks

- **Foreign net sell continuing despite green tape:** IDR 791B outflow on +1.22% IHSG day = market rebound is domestic-driven only. Sustained foreign sell pressures multi-day rallies.
- **MSCI BREN/DSSA HSC removal in May:** ~$270M tail-outflow risk if executed. LQ45 mega-caps (BBCA, BMRI, BBRI, TLKM, ASII) most exposed to broader weight cut.
- **ITMG Q1 earnings May 7 binary:** Held position with 4.81% buffer to hard-cut. Sector-consensus forecasts EPS -29.5% YoY — the print is downside-skewed.
- **IDR pressure at 17,400:** Brent reversal helps inflation but foreign sell flow + low BI reserves ($148.2B) = persistent rupiah drag. A break above 17,500 sustained could trigger BI emergency response.
- **Banking sector exit watch:** 1 strike (BBRI hard-cut May 1). One more banking failure → sector exit rule fires (close all banking positions). Currently 0 banking exposure, so risk is on re-entry timing.
- **Data infra block (yfinance/GoAPI):** ADV unverifiable for 49 of 50 watchlist tickers (only ITMG broker-verified). Gate-check Gate 7 + Gate 14 cannot fire on any new candidate. **Hard constraint on all market-open entries until ADV verification path restored.** Document if midday infra is restored.
- **Brent reversal volatility:** Mon's +5.80% spike → Tue's -5.55% reversal in 24h. Two-way energy-tape volatility makes oil-sympathy plays (MEDC, PGAS) untradeable until headline noise stabilizes.

Controlling shareholder PT Arthakencana Rayatama (AKRT) executed a 3-tranche purchase totalling 181M shares for Rp 282.526B at IDR 1,520-1,580 over May 4-6, lifting AKRT stake to 64.607%. Stock closed +2.63% to IDR 1,560 on May 6. This is the strongest insider signal surfaced this morning.
- Thesis: Distribution sector quietly bullish — analysts unanimous: 13/0/0 buy ratings, consensus PT IDR 1,605.48 (range 1,363.50 - 1,942.50). 2026 forecast revenue Rp 44.27T, EBITDA Rp 5.03T.
- Valuation: P/E and P/B not freshly surfaced; insider-buying-while-shares-trade-at-IDR-1,520-1,580 is itself an implicit valuation signal from the most-informed party.
- Catalyst: 3-day insider accumulation completed May 6; recommended in Liputan6 May 6 ("Sinyal Kuat Pengendali AKRA").
- Analyst view: 13/0/0 buy/hold/sell consensus; average PT IDR 1,605 (~+3% from current).
- Insider activity: **CONFIRMED** — controlling shareholder Rp 282.5B over 3 days at 1,520-1,580.

- 50-day MA: n/a (data infra) | 200-day MA: n/a

### Macro Regime Assessment

**Regime: EM-OUTFLOW / RISK-CAUTIOUS — but easing on multiple metrics.**

- Reasoning: Foreign net sell streak moderating: −Rp 76.39B May 7 vs −Rp 484B May 6
  vs −Rp 518B May 5 vs −Rp 3T+ Apr 30. **BBRI re-accumulation +Rp 334.8B (top-2 buy)
  contradicts pure-EM-OUTFLOW thesis.** IHSG +1.15% to 7,174.32 broke above 7,200
  intraday for first time since rally start (high 7,207). Indo 10Y eased 6.81%;
  US 10Y dropped 4.35% (−10bp); Asia broadly bid (Hang Seng +1.6%, Shanghai +0.48%,
  Nikkei record). Brent partial recovery removes oil-complex panic. IDR 17,304–17,358
  (Investing) is cleaner than 17,512 (BI Kamis) — directionally improving.
- Position sizing adjustment: max 15% per RISK-STATE.json (no relaxation YET).
  Defensive Quality track suspended (no qualifying valuation × σ data accessible —
  same constraint).
- What would shift to CONSTRUCTIVE: one full week of foreign net buy ≥ Rp 1T,
  IDR break below 17,000 sustained, IHSG holds 7,200 multiple sessions, BI dovish
  signal at May 21–22 meeting.
- Weekly-review (today 16:00 WIB) should evaluate whether to formally update the
  regime label.

### Top Candidates (score ≥ 6, deep-dive)

#### 1. ASII — Foreign net buy +Rp 2.44T cumulative thru May 13, score 7 (CANDIDATE)

**Fundamental case:**
- Thesis: PT Astra International (auto + heavy equip + financial services + agri conglomerate). LQ45 mega-cap. Foreign investors accumulated +Rp 2.44T cumulative through May 13 — the single largest single-name accumulation by foreigners during the MSCI-driven sell-off week. Remains in MSCI Global Standard Index (not affected by rebalancing churn).
- Thesis: Asymmetric flow signal: while banks (BMRI −Rp 1.41T) and big mining names (MDKA, INCO, BREN) bled foreign capital, ASII was bought into weakness. This pattern echoes BBRI re-accumulation May 7 (catalyst-track marker for institutional repositioning).
- Valuation: PE attractive vs 5-year average per typical conglomerate analyst frame (not numerically sourced this cycle).
- Catalyst: foreign flow accumulation is itself the catalyst; defensive carry into BI RDG May 21–22.
- Analyst view: (general buy bias for LQ45 mega-cap conglomerate; specific PT not sourced this cycle).
- Insider activity: (not specifically surfaced).

**Technical context:**
- Price: live mark UNVERIFIED (WebSearch returned MSCI / FX news only this cycle, no clean spot quote).
- 50-day MA / 200-day MA: not surfaced.
- Volume: ADV unverifiable (yfinance blocked); ASII is LQ45 mega-cap, ADV typically 50–100M sh — ample.
- Support / Resistance: not surfaced this cycle.
- Trend: defensive accumulation vs MSCI selloff = relative outperformer.

**Trade plan:**
- Entry: requires live-price verification at /market-open.
- Stop: −7% hard cut from entry.
- Target: +10–12% provisional pending PT.
- R:R: TBD pending entry pricing.
- Position size: 8–10% of equity (defensive carry; lower idiosyncratic-conviction than fundamental Q1 beats).
- Conviction: MEDIUM (flow-driven, not idiosyncratic earnings catalyst).
- ADV: **UNKNOWN — must verify.** ASII is LQ45 mega-cap; ample.

**Action: WATCH-promoted-to-CANDIDATE.** Pre-mortem: if foreign flow reverses (ASII single-name net sell in next 3 sessions) AND price gaps below entry × 0.96 within 5 days, thesis broken.

### Macro Regime Assessment

**Regime: EM OUTFLOW / RISK-CAUTIOUS — INTENSIFIED (reverting from "RECOVERING" stance).**

- Reasoning: One of the four "shift to RISK-NEUTRAL" triggers had been partial (foreign-flow inflection May 7). **All four reversed last week:**
  1. IDR — record-high 17,623, broke 17,500 sustained → trigger REVERSED (worse, not better).

- The "RECOVERING" stance from May 8 is INVALIDATED. Tape voted with index −3.53% and IDR record. Regime reverts to **EM-OUTFLOW / RISK-CAUTIOUS — INTENSIFIED** (one step deeper than May 8 baseline).

- Defensive Quality Track suspended (per TRADING-STRATEGY.md: "Regime is not DEFENSIVE" check fails the second the regime would labeled DEFENSIVE). Current label is EM-OUTFLOW / RISK-CAUTIOUS — INTENSIFIED, **not yet DEFENSIVE** but one notch from it. Watch BI RDG May 21–22: hawkish surprise pushes to full DEFENSIVE.

- Defensive Quality Track: SUSPENDED per TRADING-STRATEGY.md.

### Top Candidates (score ≥ 6, deep-dive required)

#### 1. BBCA — Deposit-rich BI hike beneficiary, defensive blue-chip

**Fundamental case:**
- Thesis: PT Bank Central Asia is Indonesia's deposit-rich CASA-leader (>70% CASA); on a +50bp BI hike, deposit-light banks see funding-cost pass-through faster than asset-yield reprice, but BCA's giant deposit moat shifts the asymmetry to NIM-expansion. Defensive blue-chip foreign-flow magnet during capitulation.
- Catalyst: BI delivered hawkish surprise May 20 +50bp to 5.25% (vs +25bp consensus); IDXFINANCE +1.21% intraday on the announcement — banks bid as the BI defense narrative crystallized. BCA Q1 prints already cleared; clean tape into the hike.
- Valuation: P/E ~22x (premium to sector ~10–15x), P/B ~5x (premium to sector ~1.5–2x). Defensive blue-chip premium intact; not a "cheap" name, but a flight-to-quality name in EM-OUTFLOW/DEFENSIVE.
- Analyst view: Consensus Hold-to-Buy on most desks; targets clustered around 6,400–6,700 IDR (data infra blocked — analyst-bottom-up not verifiable today; flag as caveat).
- Insider activity: Not surfaced today.

**Technical context:**
- Price: IDR 6,000 (May 20 close, +0.84% on hike day) | 50-day MA: ~6,100 est | 200-day MA: ~6,500 est (data infra blocked, est from prior research)
- Volume: above-average on bid May 20 (intraday positioning into hike)
- Support: 5,800–5,950 | Resistance: 6,150–6,250
- Trend: Range-bound consolidation off Nov 2025 peak; defensive base-building

**Trade plan:**
- Entry: 5,900–6,000 (Gate 9 ceiling ~6,180 from 6,000; below ceiling)
- Stop: 5,580 (−7% from 6,000) — HARD-CUT
- Target: 6,400 (+6.7%)
- R:R ratio: 0.96:1 at 6,000 entry (sub-2:1 → fails entry criteria; would need entry ≤ 5,800 for 2:1)
- Position size: 5–7% of equity (regime DEFENSIVE cap per MISTAKES.md 2026-05-20 lesson)
- Conviction: MEDIUM (defensive trade, not high-conviction catalyst)
- ADV: not verifiable under yfinance blackout (Day 31); BBCA is the largest IDX market-cap stock; ADV historically >30M shares — well above 500k floor. Gate 7 + 14 should pass at any sub-1B IDR position size.
- **R:R verdict:** Fails 2:1 minimum at 6,000 entry. Need pullback to ≤5,800 to qualify, OR raise target above 6,440 with conviction.

#### 3. ASII — Foreign-flow top YTD; held green on capitulation day

**Fundamental case:**
- Thesis: PT Astra International is Indonesia's dominant industrial conglomerate (auto, heavy equipment, financial services, agribusiness). Foreign accumulated net buy YTD = **+Rp2.65T** through May 13 — highest YTD foreign net buy stock in regular market. On May 19 capitulation day (IHSG −3.46%), ASII closed −0.42% only (sole big-cap green-relative; +3 percentage points outperformance). Defensive consolidation magnet.
- Catalyst: Foreign-rotation continuation into defensive industrial complex; UNTR final-div Rp 3.86T early May capital-return signal to Astra parent. ASII's UNTR mining-services arm has partial Danantara exposure but small relative to group (auto + financial services dominate revenue).

### Macro Regime Assessment

**Regime: DEFENSIVE-confirmed (4/4 shift triggers met yesterday; BI hike +50bp + Danantara confirmation = regime entrenched). Formal label flip pending weekly-review May 22.**

- Reasoning: BI delivered +50bp surprise (vs +25 consensus) = hawkish rupiah-defense priority over growth. Prabowo officially confirmed Danantara Sumberdaya single-gateway export company for coal/CPO/ferroalloys (transition Jun–Aug, full Sep) = structural sector-policy break for ~30% of IDX commodity-exporter market cap. IDR improving (17,695 vs 17,752 record) is constructive but defense was costly. IHSG at 6,318 (still below 6,400; near 1-yr lows). Regime label tightens to DEFENSIVE-confirmed; the recovery-watch is now contingent on (a) sustained IDR <17,500, (b) IHSG reclaiming 6,500 with conviction, (c) foreign-flow inflection, (d) Danantara transition execution clarity.
- Position sizing adjustment: **Max position size 7% of equity** (down from 10% per regime + MISTAKES.md 2026-05-20 lesson — wider intraday IDR volatility × tight hard-cut → noise-stops more likely; tighter sizing preserves trial alpha).
- Defensive Quality Track: **SUSPENDED** (per TRADING-STRATEGY.md — DEFENSIVE regime disables track).
- Sector exits: Coal **EXITED** (ITMG May 18 + ADRO May 20 = 2 consecutive losses). Banking sector-watch (1 of 2 strike from BBRI May 1) — BBCA entry possible since BBCA ≠ BBRI ticker and idiosyncratic catalyst differs, but strike must be respected.
- Risk implication: drawdown −2.16% from peak; cumulative trial alpha vs IHSG +15.32%. Path-fragile but constructive. Patience over activity remains the binding rule.

### Flagged Risks

- **Danantara transition ambiguity (Jun–Aug 2026)** — implementation details unclear; if monopolistic abuses emerge, coal/CPO/ferroalloy stocks face deeper structural rerate. AVOID coal/CPO entirely; partial overhang on ferroalloys/nickel.
- **BI hike second-order effects** — +50bp NIM-compresses loan-heavy banks (BMRI guidance 4.6–4.8% vs 4.89% 2025); +50bp HURTS property (mortgage demand), tech (rate-sensitive), construction (leverage cost).
- **IDR fragility** — 17,695 better than 17,752 record but still elevated; if IDR re-tests 17,750+ on tape, regime tightens to DEFENSIVE-strict (new entries paused).
- **IHSG technical** — 6,184 support (Kontan analyst); break = continuation capitulation. 6,388 resistance; reclaim = relief rally. Today's print decisive.
- **Data infra Day 31** — yfinance still blocked; all marks WebSearch multi-source; ADV unverifiable; multi-source verification BINDING for any near-stop position.
- **R:R compression on big-cap defensives** — BBCA, TLKM, ASII all show sub-2:1 R:R at current marks; only KLBF qualifies at 2.31:1. Discipline over activity binding.
- **Trades this week: 0/3 used** — patience holds. Best-case 1 entry today (KLBF) if mark verifies and IHSG opens stable.
- **Foreign flow Day 23** — MSCI rebal wave continues through May 29; passive outflow $1.6–1.8B continues to weigh.
